簇 #3 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
KERAJAAN PERPADUAN: KESTABILAN DAN REFORMASI DALAM LANDASAN POLITIK BAHARU 1.	Kerajaan Perpaduan pimpinan Perdana Menteri, YAB Dato’ Seri Anwar Ibrahim terus menunjukkan ketahanan melalui pendekatan kolaboratif antara komponen PH, BN, dan GPS. Berbanding naratif “krisis politik” yang didakwa sesetengah pihak, realiti semasa membuktikan bahawa kerajaan sekarang kekal utuh dengan sokongan majoriti yang kukuh dalam parlimen.  2.	Dalam sistem demokrasi berparlimen seperti Malaysia, kerajaan gabungan merupakan satu mekanisme biasa untuk memastikan kestabilan politik. Peletakan jawatan Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad sebenarnya mencerminkan proses demokrasi dalaman parti (PKR), bukannya petanda keruntuhan kerajaan. 3.	Geseran dalaman dalam sesebuah kerajaan gabungan adalah sesuatu yang normal. YAB Dato’ Seri Anwar Ibrahim telah menunjukkan kebijaksanaan politik dengan mengekalkan majoriti melalui perundingan berterusan antara komponen PH-BN. Pendekatan inklusif ini justeru mengukuhkan daya tahan kerajaan. 4.	Walaupun terdapat tanggapan bahawa UMNO sedang dalam proses kebangkitan semula dan berpotensi mengambil alih kuasa, data sebaliknya menunjukkan parti tersebut masih menghadapi cabaran besar. Dalam PRU-15, UMNO hanya berjaya memenangi 26 kerusi berbanding 54 kerusi pada 2018, jelas menunjukkan kemerosotan pengaruhnya dalam kalangan pengundi. 5.	Selain itu, peralihan Tengku Zafrul ke PKR pula dilihat sebagai pengukuhan kepada parti pemerintah itu, di mana beliau membawa bersama pengalaman ekonomi dan jaringan sokongan baharu yang memberi nilai tambah. UMNO masih berada dalam fasa pemulihan pasca-skandal 1MDB dan pengaruhnya dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan kini adalah terhad. 6.	Kerajaan Perpaduan telah menunjukkan komitmennya dalam melaksanakan pelbagai inisiatif reformasi. Antaranya termasuklah pelaksanaan National Anti-Corruption Plan (NACP) dan pemantauan rapi terhadap projek mega seperti LCS, yang membuktikan kesungguhan kerajaan dalam memperkukuh tadbir urus dan ketelusan.  7.	Dalam pada itu, keputusan mahkamah berkenaan kes Datuk Seri Ahmad Zahid Hamidi pula perlu dilihat sebagai proses keadilan yang berasingan daripada pengaruh politik, sekali gus mengukuhkan prinsip pengasingan kuasa dalam sistem demokrasi negara. 8.	Kerajaan Perpaduan di bawah kepimpinan Dato’ Seri Anwar Ibrahim tetap stabil dengan komitmen terhadap tadbir urus baik dan perpaduan nasional. Naratif "krisis kerajaan" dan "kebangkitan UMNO" lebih bersifat retorik politik berbanding realiti semasa. Sebagai kerajaan pertama yang menggabungkan PH-BN-GPS, model ini mencerminkan kematangan demokrasi Malaysia yang terus berkembang. #MyCommunityNews #MCN #KerajaanPerpaduan #AnalisisPolitikSemasa

簇 #4 (包含 2 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
Rafizi Ramli’s decision to resign from the Cabinet has drawn little concern from residents in Pandan, who say political shifts matter less than what is done on the ground.

While many voters remain supportive of Rafizi continuing as their Member of Parliament, they also want greater grassroots involvement and more effective attention to local problems that affect daily life.

Following his defeat in the recent PKR party elections, Rafizi stepped down from his ministerial post — but in Pandan, constituents made it clear they expect their MP to stay committed to solving issues in the area.

Many praised Rafizi for being more visible than previous MPs, yet noted that presence alone is not enough. 

📹 Fabian Peter
------------------------------
KUALA LUMPUR — Rafizi Ramli’s decision to resign from the Cabinet has drawn little concern from residents in Pandan, who say political shifts matter less than what is done on the ground.While many voters remain supportive of Rafizi continuing as their Member of Parliament, they also want greater grassroots involvement and more effective attention to local problems that affect daily life.Many praised Rafizi for being more visible than previous MPs, yet noted that presence alone is not enough.Yuen Sang, a 47-year-old freelancer who has voted in Pandan since 2008, said there has been a “slight improvement” under Rafizi’s tenure, particularly regarding roadworks

簇 #9 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
EGO SEORANG RAFIZI Usai kekalahan pada pemilihan jawatan Timbalan Presiden Parti Keadilan Rakyat pada MPP PKR 2025, Rafizi Ramli mengambil keputusan untuk melepaskan jawatannya sebagai Menteri Ekonomi pula. Pelepasan jawatan itu tidak kosong, turut disertai dengan kenyataan-kenyataan Rafizi, baik secara verbal mahupun bertulis mengenai misi dan visinya menyertai politik sebelum ini- membudayakan 'kebertanggungjawaban mandat rakyat'. Kata Rafizi, ini amalan demokrasi. Bila dah tak dapat sokongan dalam parti, maka secara automatiknya mandat yang sebelum ini digalas turut terkubur. Rafizi dan kenyataan yang berbaur ego! Mungkin Rafizi tak sedar, sebelum ni yang dia katakan sebagai 'mandat rakyat' itu dia dapatkan dengan cara licik dan tak masuk akal. Rafizi galak menghasilan sejumah 'formula-formula aneh' bagi mempengaruhi minda masyarakat untuk menolak hukum logik berlandaskan hakikat, serta kemampuan negara dan kerajaan yang mentadbir. Jika tidak, masakan Rafizi mendapat gelaran 'Raja Formula'? Sudah la bermain dengan formula yang melawan hukum akal. Apabila dipersoalkan kembali sejauh mana keberkesanan formula-formula ini, pasti individu itu akan dikritik hebat oleh Rafizi sendiri! Jawab Rafizi, "Mereka tak faham apa yang saya katakan" atau  "mereka tidak sepandai saya". Tapi tak ada yang lebih hebat apabila Rafizi memberikan reaksi, "Memang bahalol, formula sedang berjalan la bodoh!" Begitukah caranya seorang pemimpin 'bertanggungjawab ke atas mandat rakyat?' Menghina dan memperlekeh, itulah wajah sebenar Rafizi Ramli. Maka tak hairanlah jika dia tak mampu bertahan pada pemilihan kali ini. Rafizi, anda jatuh akibat sikap sendiri! Tapi satu hal yang wajar dipuji. Bila Rafizi tahu dia dah tak ada tempat, baik dalam parti mahu pun dalam kerajaan... Tak tunggu lama, cepat-cepat dia angkat kaki. Tapi tak tahulah kan, drama apa pula Rafizi akan bawa selepas ini. #MyCommunityNews #MCN #RajaFormula #RafiziRamli #EgoSeorangRafizi

簇 #11 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
On May 10, Rafizi Ramli told Malaysians he would resign as economy minister if he failed to win re-election as PKR deputy president at the party polls on May 23.True to his word, after his defeat to Nurul Izzah Anwar, Rafizi announced on May 28 that he had submitted his resignation and that it would take effect on June 17.He noted that it was the practice in nations that upheld democratic principles for party leaders who lost internal elections to resign from government posts.He said: “My defeat in the recent PKR election means I no longer have the party’s mandate to translate the people’s agenda, as championed by PKR, into government programmes.

簇 #15 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
روي عن أبي بصير قال: دخلت المسجد مع أبي جعفر عليه السلام والناس يدخلون ويخرجون فقال لي: سل الناس هل يرونني؟ فكل من لقيته قلت له: أرأيت أبا جعفر؟ يقول: لا، وهو واقف حتى دخل أبو هارون المكفوف، قال: سل هذا، فقلت: هل رأيت أبا جعفر؟ فقال: أليس هو بقائم، قال: وما علمك؟ قال: وكيف لا أعلم وهو نور ساطع Əbu Bəsir belə nəql edir: “İmam Baqirlə (ə) birlikdə məscidə daxil oldum. İnsanlar daxil olub çıxırdılar. İmam (ə) mənə buyurdu: “İnsanlardan soruş. Məni görürlərmi?” Mən qarşılaşdığım hər kəsdən soruşdum: “Əbu Cəfəri (İmam Baqiri) gördünmü?” Onlar isə “Yox” – deyirdilər. İmam (ə) isə ayaq üstə dayanmışdı. Nəhayət Harun Məkfuf içəri daxil oldu. İmam (ə) buyurdu: “Bundan da soruş”. Ondan soruşdum: “Əbu Cəfəri gördünmü?” Harun dedi: “Məgər burada dayanmayıb?” Mən soruşdum: “Haradan bildin?” Harun dedi: “Necə bilməyim ki, o, parlaq bir nurdur”. Şeyx Qutbuddin Ravəndi, “əl-Xəraic vəl-Cəraih”, cild 2, səhifə 595 və 596, hədis 7. #nur #şiə #rafizi #əxbari #təcəlla #təcəlli

簇 #33 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
[KiniNews] Zaid Ibrahim has urged PAS to exhaust all avenues to court former PKR deputy president Rafizi Ramli and proposed that the party field him in Tambun - the parliamentary seat in Perak held by Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahim.

The ex-law minister also encouraged the Islamist party to approach former PKR vice-president Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad, suggesting that he contest in Bentong, which is DAP MP Young Syefura Othman’s seat.

“Both are good leaders, and any political party will find them helpful. PAS should try to persuade them to be their candidates for the next general election," he said.

Meanwhile, in a separate story, The Kuala Lumpur High Court has denied Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahim’s bid to suspend the civil lawsuit brought by Yusoff Rawther, who has accused him of sexual assault.

In delivering her ruling today, High Court judge Roz Mawar Rozain also stated that the court had found the eight constitutional questions Anwar had sought to refer to the Federal Court did not meet the required threshold.

Anwar has clarified that it was not about seeking personal immunity, but to ensure that high public office is protected from litigation that may be strategically timed, politically motivated, or institutionally disruptive.

簇 #34 (包含 2 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
Bekas Timbalan Presiden PKR, Rafizi Ramli, hari ini berkongsi pandangannya mengenai cara membuat keputusan dalam kehidupan seharian, di tengah-tengah spekulasi mengenai hala tuju politiknya selepas tewas dalam pemilihan parti baru-baru ini. “Kita buat macam-macam keputusan setiap hari, ada keputusan besar, ada keputusan kecil. Petua saya dalam membuat keputusan: Bukan mengenai apa yang kita mahu, tetapi mengenai apa yang perlu dilakukan,” katanya dalam satu hantaran di media sosial. Rafizi yang meletak jawatan sebagai Menteri Ekonomi selepas tewas dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, masih belum mendedahkan perancangannya. Belum dapat dipastikan apakah hantaran terbaru itu ada kaitan dengan kerjaya politiknya atau sekadar luahan biasa. Rafizi dalam satu hantaran di platform X minggu lalu berkata beliau akan berkongsi mengenai perancangannya selepas sambutan Hari Raya Aidiladha yang dijangka jatuh pada 7 Jun. Dalam satu hantaran di X minggu lalu, Rafizi berkata: “Saya dah rancang apa nak fokus lepas ini, tapi beri masa semua orang bertenang dulu, dengan sambutan Hari Raya Haji dan sebagainya.” “Apa-apa saya kongsi kemudian. Potensi sebenar negara adalah rakyat biasa. Kita perlu kembali bangunkan potensi itu.” Dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, Rafizi tewas kepada Nurul Izzah, anak kepada perdana menteri dan Presiden PKR, Anwar Ibrahim. Penyertaan Nurul Izzah dalam pemilihan parti itu telah menimbulkan dakwaan berlakunya amalan nepotisme dalam PKR. Bagaimanapun, Anwar menafikan dakwaan tersebut dan menegaskan bahawa proses pemilihan dijalankan secara demokratik serta terbuka kepada semua ahli parti. Nurul Izzah, anak kepada Presiden PKR merangkap Perdana Menteri, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim, memperoleh 9,803 undi daripada kira-kira 15,000 perwakilan yang mengundi secara fizikal dan dalam talian.
------------------------------
Bekas timbalan presiden PKR, Rafizi Ramli, hari ini berkongsi 'petuanya' dalam membuat keputusan.“Kita buat macam-macam keputusan setiap hari, ada keputusan besar, ada keputusan kecil. Petua saya dalam membuat keputusan: Bukan mengenai apa yang kita mahu, tetapi mengenai apa yang perlu dilakukan,” katanya dalam satu hantaran di media sosial.Rafizi yang meletak jawatan sebagai Menteri Ekonomi selepas tewas dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, masih belum mendedahkan perancangannya.Belum dapat dipastikan apakah hantaran terbaru itu ada kaitan dengan kerjaya politiknya atau sekadar luahan biasa.Sebelum ini, ahli parlimen Pandan itu berkata dia akan berkongsi lebih banyak mengenai perancangannya selepas Hari Raya Aidiladha (7 Jun).Dalam satu hantaran di X minggu lalu, Rafizi berkata: “Saya dah rancang apa nak fokus lepas ini, tapi beri masa semua orang bertenang dulu, dengan sambutan Hari Raya Haji dan sebagainya.”“Apa-apa saya kongsi kemudian. Potensi sebenar negara adalah rakyat biasa. Kita perlu kembali bangunkan potensi itu,”Dalam pemilihan PKR baru-baru ini, Rafizi tewas kepada Nurul Izzah, anak kepada perdana menteri dan Presiden PKR, Anwar Ibrahim.Langkah Nurul Izzah menyertai persaingan merebut jawatan nombor dua dalam PKR itu menimbulkan dakwaan PKR mengamalkan nepotisme.Anwar menafikan dakwaan itu dan menegaskan Nurul Izzah dipilih secara demokrasi oleh ahli parti.Nurul Izzah memperoleh 9,803 undi daripada kira-kira 15,000 perwakilan yang mengundi secara fizikal dan dalam talian
------------------------------

簇 #41 (包含 2 条文档)

Syed SaddiqSHAH ALAM - Muar MP Syed Saddiq Syed Abdul Rahman believes that a person's political journey is long and not defined by a single political cycle.His comments come after the recent resignations of Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli and Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad.Rafizi (left) and Nik Nazmi.Syed Saddiq, who is well aware of the unpredictable nature of politics, spoke about the enduring nature of political careers and the importance of continued public service, regardless of formal titles.“That is their choice and I respect it. I know both of them and I believe they are good leaders for Malaysia,” he said told Sinar Daily at the RoadTour SPM PTTI event held at the Ideal Convention Centre here today.He pointed out that political careers are rarely straightforward or confined to one election or term."A person's political journey is usually very long. It’s not just defined by one political cycle."From the bottom of my heart, I wish them all the best. Wherever they go, whether in or out of government, I’m confident they’ll find the best ways to serve the interests of all Malaysians," he added.When asked about perceptions of nepotism or internal party dynamics within PKR, Syed Saddiq chose not to comment in detail but reflected on his own experiences.“I’m not going to speak about nepotism or such issues, that’s an internal party matter. But I can speak from my own personal experience in 2018,” he said.Recalling his time working alongside then-Deputy Prime Minister Datuk Seri Dr Wan Azizah Wan Ismail, Syed Saddiq addressed earlier allegations suggesting she was simply a "seat warmer" for her husband, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim.“In 2018, there were allegations saying that the then-Deputy Prime Minister, Wan Azizah, was only there because of Datuk Seri Anwar."But when I worked with her, it was the opposite. I truly believe she was there based on her own merit,” Syed Saddiq recalled.He praised Wan Azizah’s dedication and hard work during her tenure.“She’s an exceptional woman...super hardworking. I remember being in many meetings with her where she spoke passionately about defending the welfare of children and women, even making difficult decisions to ensure Malaysians lead healthier lives,” he said.On May 28, Rafizi officially resigned as Economy Minister, following his defeat in the PKR party elections, stating he no longer had a mandate to continue advancing the party’s agenda in the government.Shortly after, Nik Nazmi announced his resignation as Natural Resources and Environmental Sustainability Minister, effective July 4, citing his loss in the PKR elections and noting that his Cabinet role was closely tied to his former position as a party vice president.Download Sinar Daily application.Click Here!
------------------------------
SHAH ALAM - Muar MP Syed Saddiq Syed Abdul Rahman believes that a person's political journey is long and not defined by a single political cycle.  His comments come after the recent resignations of Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli and Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad.    Syed Saddiq, who is well aware of the unpredictable nature of politics, spoke about the enduring nature of political careers and the importance of continued public service, regardless of formal titles.  “That is their choice and I respect it. I know both of them and I believe they are good leaders for Malaysia,” he said told Sinar Daily at the RoadTour SPM PTTI event held at the Ideal Convention Centre here today.  He pointed out that political careers are rarely straightforward or confined to one election or term.  "A person's political journey is usually very long. It’s not just defined by one political cycle.  "From the bottom of my heart, I wish them all the best. Wherever they go, whether in or out of government, I’m confident they’ll find the best ways to serve the interests of all Malaysians," he added.  When asked about perceptions of nepotism or internal party dynamics within PKR, Syed Saddiq chose not to comment in detail but reflected on his own experiences.  “I’m not going to speak about nepotism or such issues, that’s an internal party matter. But I can speak from my own personal experience in 2018,” he said.  Recalling his time working alongside then-Deputy Prime Minister Datuk Seri Dr Wan Azizah Wan Ismail, Syed Saddiq addressed earlier allegations suggesting she was simply a "seat warmer" for her husband, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim.  “In 2018, there were allegations saying that the then-Deputy Prime Minister, Wan Azizah, was only there because of Datuk Seri Anwar.  "But when I worked with her, it was the opposite. I truly believe she was there based on her own merit,” Syed Saddiq recalled.  He praised Wan Azizah’s dedication and hard work during her tenure.  “She’s an exceptional woman...super hardworking. I remember being in many meetings with her where she spoke passionately about defending the welfare of children and women, even making difficult decisions to ensure Malaysians lead healthier lives,” he said.  On May 28, Rafizi officially resigned as Economy Minister, following his defeat in the PKR party elections, stating he no longer had a mandate to continue advancing the party’s agenda in the government.  Shortly after, Nik Nazmi announced his resignation as Natural Resources and Environmental Sustainability Minister, effective July 4, citing his loss in the PKR elections and noting that his Cabinet role was closely tied to his former position as a party vice president.
------------------------------

簇 #43 (包含 1 条文档)

Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR) perlu segera membina semula kekuatan pasca-pemilihan peringkat pusat bagi mengukuhkan keyakinan rakyat terhadap parti.

Itu pendapat dua srikandi KEADILAN, saudari Yong Bazilah Abu Bakar dan saudari Siti Aishah Shaik Ismail. Mereka turut merasakan ada ruang untuk yang kalah, seperti bekas Timbalan Presiden, Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli, untuk terus berbakti kepada parti dan negara.

Episod ini dihoskan oleh saudara Daniel Teoh.

#Channel10 #Ngopi #PKR

簇 #45 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
“Di Malaysia, kita sebenarnya dah kena bezakan untuk kelancaran jentera kerajaan, politik kepartian dan urus tadbir dipihak eksekutif kalau tidak ia akan jadi kacau,” katanya, kepada politiko.my.

Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad masing-masing meletak jawatan sebagai Menteri Ekonomi dan Menteri Sumber Asli dan Kelestarian Alam (NRES) minggu lepas susulan tewas dalam pemilihan PKR.

Rafizi gagal mempertahankan jawatan timbalan presiden dan tewas kepada anak Perdana Menteri Nurul Izzah Anwar manakala Nik Nazmi pula gagal mempertahankan jawatan naib presiden parti itu.

“Tidak timbul soal Rafizi perlu letak jawatan kerana tidak dapat mandat parti, mandat rakyat yang mengundi dia masih ada, yang undi dia di Pandan bukan ahli parti PKR, rakyat tak memihak kepada parti pun, dan dia sah. Alasan itu tidak cukup kuat untuk beliau meletak jawatan.

“Nik Nazmi juga memberi alasan sama kerana tak dapat pertahankan jawatan naib presiden, kemudian mungkin kerana dia memihak kepada Rafizi dalam pertandingan antara kem,” katanya, dan menegaskan tindakan itu bukan satu keperluan.

Jelasnya, tindakan diambil dua bekas menteri itu merugikan negara
------------------------------


簇 #46 (包含 3 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------

Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahim’s plan to build a new hi-tech city named after his “Madani” slogan has sparked fresh outrage, with Malaysians accusing the government of splurging on a vanity project while imposing spending cuts on the public.\nAnwar rose to power in 2022 on the promise that he would avoid the excesses of his predecessors. He vowed to stamp out corruption and cronyism after years of scandals that cost the country billions of dollars.\nHis credibility has taken several blows since then, however. The most recent came late last month with the resignation of two cabinet ministers over a nepotism row, which erupted after his daughter, Nurul Izzah, was elected deputy president of his ruling People’s Justice Party (PKR).\nOn Tuesday, the prime minister announced plans for a new “Madani City” within the administrative capital of Putrajaya, replete with schools, healthcare and public transport for more than 30,000 people.\nMadani City “will focus on comprehensive and centralised facilities for the welfare of the people”, Anwar said in a statement.\n\nThe first phase of the city, named after his administration’s tagline – a Malay word that translates to “civilisation” – is set for completion by the end of 2027, featuring 3,000 homes and a secondary school. Anwar did not disclose the total cost of the project or its funding sources.\nHis announcement quickly triggered a flurry of criticism on social media, with many questioning the government’s priorities. Wage earners are struggling with rising costs alongside cuts to state subsidies for electricity and diesel, which Anwar argued were essential for reducing government spending.\n“There is so much government infrastructure that is broken down and in need of repairs. But the government prefers to spend money on wasteful megaprojects like this,” one response to Anwar’s social media post read.\nOthers highlighted Malaysia’s ongoing shortage of doctors due to federal budget constraints.\nIt should be called ‘Nepotism City’\nReply to Anwar’s social media post\n“It should be called ‘Nepotism City’,” remarked another reply, reflecting public sentiment regarding the political turmoil within the PKR that led to the resignations Economy Minister Rafizi Ramli and Environment Minister Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad.\nAnwar’s reputation as a reform icon has taken a beating since he took office three years ago. Numerous leaders from coalition partner and erstwhile rival Umno have been granted reprieves from corruption trials, notably Umno president and Deputy Prime Minister Ahmad Zahid Hamidi.\n\nMalaysia’s prime minister has also faced mounting public opprobrium for slashing costly subsidies to bring down the country’s debt of more than 1 trillion ringgit (US$235 million).\nLast July, the government cut diesel subsidies at the pump and limited the list of eligible recipients, a move projected to save more than 7 billion ringgit from its annual subsidy bill.\nThe government announced last month that it planned to restructure subsidies on petrol – Malaysia’s most widely used fuel – in the latter half of this year.\nAt the same time, Anwar has been promoting various projects under his government tagline, including “Residensi Madani”, a programme offering medium-cost housing for first-time homebuyers.\nIn March, a private developer announced that a new mosque to be built in the heart of Kuala Lumpur would be named the Madani Mosque after the government intervened to settle a controversial ownership dispute with a Hindu temple.\n“This Madani is such a headache. As long as the name Madani is there everything is on … yet we don’t know what exactly they are doing for the people’s welfare,” Kamal Bhai wrote in response to Anwar’s post.\
------------------------------

簇 #47 (包含 2 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
This article first appeared in The Edge Malaysia Weekly on May 26, 2025 - June 1, 2025THE European Investment Bank (EIB), the lending arm of the European Union (EU), is keen to participate in more infrastructure-related investments in Malaysia and is open to expanding its reach here.

According to sources, EIB is currently in discussions with the Ministry of Finance (MoF) to set up a legal framework to expand activity in the country, particularly in the Johor-Singapore Special Economic Zone (JS-SEZ).

When contacted, an EIB spokesperson confirms the bank is open to exploring investment opportunities in Malaysia. However, the bank rules out any immediate plans for a dedicated EIB office in Kuala Lumpur, and will maintain its operations at its regional hub in Jakarta.

The EIB, which is one of the world’s largest multilateral financial institutions, opened its regional representation office for Southeast Asia and the Pacific in Jakarta in September 2022.

The EIB spokesperson emphasised that formalising a country framework agreement would be a critical first step towards establishing the legal basis for EIB’s operations in Malaysia.

“Once such an agreement is in place, we would be pleased to engage with both public and private sector stakeholders to explore and develop a pipeline of potential investments,” the spokesperson says.

The move aligns with the EU’s ambitious Global Gateway strategy, which aims to boost smart, clean and secure links in the digital, energy and transport sectors, and to strengthen health, education and research systems worldwide. EIB typically focuses its financing on projects in sustainable infrastructure, the green energy transition, climate resilience, digitalisation and innovation.

Depending on the sector and project readiness, EIB says its investments can range from long-term sovereign or municipal lending to direct financing or intermediated loans through partner banks, particularly for private sector initiatives that contribute to the green and digital transitions.

“Malaysia is an important partner for the EU,” the EIB spokesperson says. “As the bank of the EU, we are open to engaging with Malaysian authorities to explore opportunities for future collaboration.”

In April, the EU ambassador to Malaysia Rafael Daerr expressed interest in future funding support via loans, grants or financial guarantees as well as potential EIB investments for the Lumut Maritime Industrial City (LuMIC) in Perak.

“That decision has not been finalised, but the LuMIC project aligns with the EU’s goals under our Global Gateway strategy. It has the potential to become a high-standard, mutually beneficial gateway between Malaysia and Europe,” Daerr reportedly said at the LuMIC Masterplan launch on April 10.

The LuMIC project — one of Perak’s five regional growth nodes identified under the Perak Sejahtera 2030 blueprint — has completed early-stage feasibility and spatial studies, funded by a €1.9 million (RM9.2 million) grant from EU.

Daerr also mentioned discussions between EIB and MoF for the bank to set up a framework in the country.

Presently, there are several European banks in the country, including Deutsche Bank and BNP Paribas. Deutsche Bank has been operating in Malaysia for over 55 years, with offices in Kuala Lumpur and Labuan, its website shows. BNP Paribas has a locally incorporated subsidiary, BNP Paribas Malaysia Bhd.

While MoF has yet to respond to The Edge’s queries as at press time, Minister of Economy Datuk Seri Mohd Rafizi Ramli last week hinted at ongoing discussions with a “European bank” to attract investments for JS-SEZ.

“We have one European bank that we have been talking to for a while. I think they will come on board. They have been working with us. It’s just that I think it takes slightly longer to go through the internal process, so the banks will plan and will develop their own programme themselves,” Rafizi said during his keynote address at the JS-SEZ Partners’ Dialogue: Advancing Facilitation session on May 19.

At the event, six major local and international banks signed letters of intent with the Ministry of Economy to help bring investments to JS-SEZ. A total of RM2.35 billion in investment interest had already been secured. The signatories were Malayan Banking Bhd (KL:MAYBANK), CIMB Group Holdings Bhd (KL:CIMB), CGS International, Sumitomo Mitsui Banking Malaysia, Bank of America Malaysia and HSBC Malaysia.

Rafizi said the banks will realise the vision of JS-SEZ through financing support, promotion, stakeholder engagement and market intelligence. He noted that the lenders will have direct access to government policy and support to convince their clients to invest in the zone. The banks were picked to ensure broad international investor outreach, with CGS International targeting Chinese investors, Sumitomo Mitsui covering East Asia, and Bank of America representing the US market, he said.

This article first appeared in The Edge Malaysia Weekly on May 26, 2025 - June 1, 2025THE European Investment Bank (EIB), the lending arm of the European Union (EU), is keen to participate in more infrastructure-related investments in Malaysia and is open to expanding its reach here.

According to sources, EIB is currently in discussions with the Ministry of Finance (MoF) to set up a legal framework to expand activity in the country, particularly in the Johor-Singapore Special Economic Zone (JS-SEZ).

When contacted, an EIB spokesperson confirms the bank is open to exploring investment opportunities in Malaysia. However, the bank rules out any immediate plans for a dedicated EIB office in Kuala Lumpur, and will maintain its operations at its regional hub in Jakarta.

The EIB, which is one of the world’s largest multilateral financial institutions, opened its regional representation office for Southeast Asia and the Pacific in Jakarta in September 2022.

The EIB spokesperson emphasised that formalising a country framework agreement would be a critical first step towards establishing the legal basis for EIB’s operations in Malaysia.

“Once such an agreement is in place, we would be pleased to engage with both public and private sector stakeholders to explore and develop a pipeline of potential investments,” the spokesperson says.

The move aligns with the EU’s ambitious Global Gateway strategy, which aims to boost smart, clean and secure links in the digital, energy and transport sectors, and to strengthen health, education and research systems worldwide. EIB typically focuses its financing on projects in sustainable infrastructure, the green energy transition, climate resilience, digitalisation and innovation.

Depending on the sector and project readiness, EIB says its investments can range from long-term sovereign or municipal lending to direct financing or intermediated loans through partner banks, particularly for private sector initiatives that contribute to the green and digital transitions.

“Malaysia is an important partner for the EU,” the EIB spokesperson says. “As the bank of the EU, we are open to engaging with Malaysian authorities to explore opportunities for future collaboration.”

In April, the EU ambassador to Malaysia Rafael Daerr expressed interest in future funding support via loans, grants or financial guarantees as well as potential EIB investments for the Lumut Maritime Industrial City (LuMIC) in Perak.

“That decision has not been finalised, but the LuMIC project aligns with the EU’s goals under our Global Gateway strategy. It has the potential to become a high-standard, mutually beneficial gateway between Malaysia and Europe,” Daerr reportedly said at the LuMIC Masterplan launch on April 10.

The LuMIC project — one of Perak’s five regional growth nodes identified under the Perak Sejahtera 2030 blueprint — has completed early-stage feasibility and spatial studies, funded by a €1.9 million (RM9.2 million) grant from EU.

Daerr also mentioned discussions between EIB and MoF for the bank to set up a framework in the country.

Presently, there are several European banks in the country, including Deutsche Bank and BNP Paribas. Deutsche Bank has been operating in Malaysia for over 55 years, with offices in Kuala Lumpur and Labuan, its website shows. BNP Paribas has a locally incorporated subsidiary, BNP Paribas Malaysia Bhd.

While MoF has yet to respond to The Edge’s queries as at press time, Minister of Economy Datuk Seri Mohd Rafizi Ramli last week hinted at ongoing discussions with a “European bank” to attract investments for JS-SEZ.

“We have one European bank that we have been talking to for a while. I think they will come on board. They have been working with us. It’s just that I think it takes slightly longer to go through the internal process, so the banks will plan and will develop their own programme themselves,” Rafizi said during his keynote address at the JS-SEZ Partners’ Dialogue: Advancing Facilitation session on May 19.

At the event, six major local and international banks signed letters of intent with the Ministry of Economy to help bring investments to JS-SEZ. A total of RM2.35 billion in investment interest had already been secured. The signatories were Malayan Banking Bhd (KL:MAYBANK), CIMB Group Holdings Bhd (KL:CIMB), CGS International, Sumitomo Mitsui Banking Malaysia, Bank of America Malaysia and HSBC Malaysia.

Rafizi said the banks will realise the vision of JS-SEZ through financing support, promotion, stakeholder engagement and market intelligence. He noted that the lenders will have direct access to government policy and support to convince their clients to invest in the zone. The banks were picked to ensure broad international investor outreach, with CGS International targeting Chinese investors, Sumitomo Mitsui covering East Asia, and Bank of America representing the US market, he said.

簇 #58 (包含 9 条文档)

Nama Datuk Seri Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz kini hangat diperkatakan dalam arena politik Selangor apabila seorang aktivis Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR), Fairul al-Qasas tampil memuji kredibiliti  beliau dan menyifatkannya sebagai tokoh paling layak untuk diangkat sebagai Menteri Besar negeri itu. Kewibawaan Tengku Zafrul sudah terbukti Memetik laporan daripada Malaysia Gazette, Fairul yang juga bekas Ketua Penerangan Cabang PKR Kuala Krau menyatakan kewibawaan beliau sudah terbukti sepanjang memegang jawatan sebagai Menteri Perdagangan, Pelaburan dan Industri (MITI), malah turut mendapat pengiktirafan daripada Perdana Menteri sendiri, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim. “Persoalan sama ada beliau mahu diangkat sebagai MB Selangor atau jadi calon PKR PRU-16 tidak sepatutnya jadi isu,” ujarnya. Penyertaan Tengku Zafrul dianggap tepat Tambahnya lagi, penyertaan Tengku Zafrul ke dalam PKR juga dilihat tepat pada masanya dan dibuat dengan cara yang betul – bukan untuk mengejar jawatan, tetapi sebagai langkah menyumbang secara berstruktur dalam parti. “Kemasukan beliau juga sesuai kerana dibuat selepas pemilihan PKR yang bermakna beliau tidak berhasrat merebut jawatan. “Jika beliau bertanding dalam pemilihan Keadilan 2028 nanti bermaksud beliau sudah tiga tahun dalam parti dan melepasi tempoh yang ditetapkan,” katanya lagi. Desas-desus Tengku Zafrul jadi MB Selangor semakin kencang Desas-desus mengenai potensi Tengku Zafrul menjadi Menteri Besar Selangor semakin kencang susulan pengumuman beliau meninggalkan UMNO dan menyatakan hasrat menyertai PKR. Ini ditambah pula dengan fakta bahawa tempoh beliau sebagai Senator akan berakhir awal Disember ini. MB Selangor nadi kosongkan kerusi DUN Walau bagaimanapun, Menteri Besar Selangor sedia ada, Datuk Seri Amirudin Shari semalam tampil menafikan akan berlaku kekosongan kerusi DUN Sungai Tua dalam masa terdekat bagi memberi laluan kepada individu tertentu bertanding. Dalam pada itu, Fairul percaya langkah politik Tengku Zafrul telah dirancang lebih awal dan berkemungkinan besar mendapat restu pemimpin kanan kedua-dua parti utama dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan. “Maka, ia juga memberi ruang Anwar untuk melantik menteri baharu bersama dua kekosongan menteri yang ditinggalkan Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad,” katanya. Walaupun menyambut baik penghijrahan Tengku Zafrul ke dalam PKR, Fairul mengingatkan agar parti itu kekal menjadi wadah inklusif untuk rakyat dan tidak berubah menjadi eksklusif untuk golongan elit semata-mata. Dalam masa sama, beliau turut menyarankan agar wakil daripada UMNO diberi ruang mengisi kekosongan di MITI bagi mengekalkan kestabilan dalam Kerajaan Perpaduan yang dibina bersama. Sumber: Malaysia Gazette (Khuzairi Ismail)
------------------------------
DATUK Seri Tengku Zafrul perlu melepaskan jawatan daripada Kabinet apabila beliau membuat keputusan keluar dari UMNO dan menyertai PKR. Pengarah Lajnah Undang-Undang dan Hak Asasi Manusia (LUHAM) Pas Selangor, Yusfarizal Yussoff berkata, tindakan Tengku Zafrul itu boleh dianggap sebagai lompat parti kerana kedudukan beliau dalam Kabinet adalah atas kapasiti UMNO    Katanya, jelas dari sudut moral politik beliau telah keluar daripada Umno, iaitu parti yang mencadangkannya untuk dilantik sebagai senator dan menteri.   “Maka keluarnya daripada Umno bermaksud, beliau sudah tidak mewakili Umno di dalam kerajaan minoriti Perpaduan tersebut,” ujar pengamal undang-undang itu,” katanya. Yusfarizal mengulas isu-isu semasa berkaitan kedudukan menteri kabinet, antaranya Menteri Ekonomi, Datuk Seri Mohd Rafizi Ramli, dan Menteri Pelaburan, Perdagangan dan Industri, Tengku Datuk Seri Zafrul Abdul Aziz.    Related Articles               Tun Mahathir Disambut Meriah di Tokyo, Teguh Perjuang Dasar Pandang ke Timur  3 June 2025               “Datang Tak Diundang, Pergi Tak Dikesali” – UMNO Sindir Zafrul  3 June 2025        Beliau berkata, tindakan mendesak Rafizi untuk meletak jawatan hanya kerana hilang jawatan dalam parti tidak tepat kerana pelantikan menteri dibuat atas syor Perdana Menteri, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim (PMX) dan perkenan Yang di-Pertuan Agong, Sultan Ibrahim.   “Saya boleh bersetuju sekiranya beliau mengambil keputusan meletak jawatan atas dasar sedar diri, namun untuk menyatakan beliau sudah tidak ada mandat, saya merasakan agak pelik. Tambahan pula, beliau masih ahli PKR,” katanya. Kes Rafizi Ramli katanya, ialah kes ‘sedar diri’ kerana sudah tidak berjawatan tinggi dalam parti walaupun pelik dari segi konsep mandat menteri, sementara kes Tengku Zafrul adalah kes ‘lompat parti’ walaupun beliau hanyalah senator lantikan.    “Ia perlu dibezakan. Adalah sedikit janggal untuk PMX menyatakan kedudukan menteri Tengku Zafrul tidak terjejas kerana ia adalah satu tindakan ‘lompat parti’. Yang lebih pelik ialah lompatan itu adalah kepada parti gabungan dalam kerajaan minoriti,” katanya. Yusfarizal turut mempersoalkan kenyataan Perdana Menteri yang menyatakan kedudukan Tengku Zafrul tidak terjejas, sedangkan tindakan berpindah parti, walaupun ke parti komponen kerajaan sendiri, tetap memberi implikasi kepada keabsahan moral pelantikan tersebut. Justeru, beliau menegaskan bahawa apa-apa prinsip dari sistem Westminster yang tidak diperuntukkan secara jelas dalam Perlembagaan harus diketepikan jika ia bertentangan dengan undang-undang tertinggi negara. Terdahulu, Tengku Zafrul keluar Umno dan menyertai PKR akan memberi kesan simbolik dan politik yang besar, khususnya kepada dinamika dalaman kerajaan campuran terutama dalam beberapa aspek.    Penolong Setiausaha Agung PAS, Khairul Faizi Ahmad Kamil berkata, pengumuman itu sebaliknya sudah dijangka susulan beberapa ramalan dan desas-desus yang tular sebelum ini. “Ditambah lagi, apabila dua kekosongan kerusi Menteri yang bakal ditinggalkan oleh Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad (terdahulu Menteri Sumber Asli dan Kelestarian Alam) memberikan ruang yang lebih luas kepada Tengku Zafrul untuk mengisi kekosongan tersebut, khususnya Menteri Ekonomi. “Sebagai Majlis Kerja Tertinggi (MKT) dan Ketua Bahagian Umno, ‘pengorbanan’ yang dibuat oleh Tengku Zafrul sudah semestinya sesuatu yang perlu digantikan dengan kedudukan yang lebih bermakna,” katanya. – SM     PENTING 1) Sertai Group Whatsapp Suara Merdeka klik dan; 2) Ikuti Suara Merdeka di Facebook, Twitter, Instagram serta TikTok! Ketika Khairy Jamaluddin sudah menjenamakan semula dirinya lebih daripada sekadar ahli politik, muncul cakap-cakap politik yang mendakwa bekas menteri dan ketua Pemuda Umno itu bakal menyertai kabinet.Dia seolah-olah menjadi orang terbuang sebelum dipecat daripada Umno pada akhir Jan 2023 selepas berseteru dengan presiden parti itu, Ahmad Zahid Hamidi. Sebelum itu – ketika PRU – dia dibawa keluar dari kerusi selamat di Rembau, Negeri Sembilan untuk bertanding di kerusi selamat untuk PH, Sungai Buloh. Walaupun memberikan saingan sengit, Khairy gagal merampas kerusi berkenaan.Dia kalah kepada bekas Bendahari Agung MIC, R Ramanan, yang bertanding sebagai calon PKR-PH.  Penganalisis politik, P Sivamurugan Pandian, menganggap khabar angin Khairy akan kembali sebagai menteri sebagai simbol usaha pemodenan dan penjenamaan semula Umno bagi menarik pengundi muda, pengundi bandar dan kelompok sederhana.Ahli akademik di Universiti Sains Malaysia itu berpendapat andainya pemimpin Umno bersedia menerima semula Khairy, 49, dan tidak menganggap tokoh itu sebagai ancaman, ia boleh menjadi langkah pendamai untuk merapatkan jurang dalam parti.“Khairy dilihat sebagai individu yang pandai berbicara, progresif dan memahami isu semasa. “Namun, dia perlu meyakinkan barisan pemimpin lama supaya mereka tidak melihatnya sebagai ancaman, sebaliknya rakan dalam perjuangan parti dan negara,” katanya kepada Malaysiakini.Sivamurugan PandianSivamurugan juga menyatakan Khairy sudah membentuk naratif – dan mendapat pengiktirafan kukuh – melalui media namun peranan sebagai menteri memerlukan tokoh berkenaan lebih daripada itu.Khairy, kata Sivamurugan, perlu menunjukkan kesanggupan politik, dinamik dan mendapat kepercayaan orang ramai.“Ia juga boleh dilihat sebagai kesediaan kerajaan untuk memberi peluang kedua dan menghargai merit melalui pendekatan yang lebih inklusif, pragmatik dan berorientasikan reformasi,” katanya.Menurut Sivamurugan lagi, jika peluang yang disebut-sebut itu muncul, Khairy wajar melihatnya sebagai kemunculan semula daripada "cuti politik" seperti yang pernah dilalui oleh bapa mentuanya, Allahyarham Abdullah Ahmad Badawi.Jika ada pertembunganUntuk rekod, suatu ketika dulu Abdullah pernah ‘terbuang’ daripada arus perdana Umno di sebalik jawatannya yang kanan dalam parti itu ekoran memilih untuk bersama kem Tengku Razaleigh Hamzah – yang mencabar Dr Mahathir Mohamad – pada 1987.Di sebalik posisinya sebagai naib presiden, Abdullah hanya menyertai kabinet tiga tahun kemudian sebelum menjadi perdana menteri pada 2003.Ketua penyelidikan di firma O2 Research, Anis Anwar, berkata reaksi rakyat terhadap khabar angin kemasukan semula Khairy ke kabinet bergantung kepada peranan yang bakal dimainkan.“Kemasukan semula Khairy mungkin sekadar mengisi kekosongan yang ditinggalkan Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz, menjadikan pelantikan itu sebagai penyelesaian sementara dan bukan penegasan reformasi jangka panjang.Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz“Namun, jika Umno mengambil peluang ini untuk menaikkan semula Khairy ke lapisan kepimpinan utama, itu menunjukkan kesediaan mereka mengembalikan dia sebagai tokoh penting parti,” katanya.Anis berkata, kemasukan Khairy akan menjadi ujian segera sama ada kabinet dan Perdana Menteri Anwar Ibrahim boleh menyesuaikan visinya dalam pentadbiran harian.“Sekiranya berlaku pertembungan, rakyat mungkin memihak kepada Khairy dan ini boleh memberi kesan kepada modal politik kerajaan. “Namun jika prestasi kerajaan meningkat dengan kehadiran Khairy, perbandingan antara ‘sebelum Khairy’ dan ‘selepas Khairy’ akan berpihak kepada beliau (Anwar).“Hanya jika perdana menteri berjaya menampilkan kejayaan itu sebagai hasil kolektif kabinet melalui agenda reformasi Madani, barulah kerajaan akan mendapat manfaat lebih besar,” katanya.Anis juga berpendapat, walaupun Khairy boleh mengisi kekosongan yang ditinggalkan Menteri Ekonomi Rafizi Ramli dan Menteri Sumber Asli dan Kelestarian Alam Sekitar Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad, ia mungkin hanya bersifat sementara.[Baca berita penuh

簇 #63 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
WAWANCARA | Berdepan pemilihan parti pada muktamar tahun ini, PAS diminta mengelakkan sebarang pertembungan tajam di peringkat tertinggi yang berisiko memberi kesan negatif kepada parti.Berkongsi pandangan peribadi, Naib Presiden PAS Mohd Amar Abdullah berkata, jika Presiden PAS Abdul Hadi Awang memilih untuk berundur sekali pun, posisi itu mesti diganti oleh timbalannya.Pun begitu, Mohd Amar berkata, pada pandangannya pilihan terbaik ialah mengekalkan Abdul Hadi bersama Tuan Ibrahim Tuan Man selaku timbalan presiden.Apa yang perlu dilakukan, kata bekas timbalan Menteri Besar Kelantan itu lagi, PAS perlu ‘menyusun’ keanggotaan di peringkat ahli Jawatankuasa PAS Pusat supaya semua kebolehan yang ada – iaitu tokoh agamawan, profesional dan teknokrat – dapat digabungkan.“Sebabnya, (jika gabungan itu wujud) banyak perkara boleh dibincangkan dalam mesyuarat PAS Pusat. Di situlah mereka boleh berikan input-input berkaitan."Di peringkat naib presiden pun dah comel gabungan antara ulama dan bukan ulama. Justeru kita perkemas di peringkat ahli jawatankuasa.“Yang pimpinan atas biar kekal, itu pandangan saya."Dan kalaulah kalau Tok Guru (Abdul Hadi) kata nak berundur, bagi saya, timbalan kena naik. Jangan ada orang lain nak pintas sebab struktur (parti) kita dah begitu.“Kalau buat begitu, nampak tenang dalam parti,” katanya dalam sesi wawancara bersama Malaysiakini di Kota Bharu, semalam.Dakwa cuba ‘langgar presiden’Mohd Amar yang juga Adun Panchor menjelaskan kalau ada pertembungan di peringkat jawatan tertinggi, akan ada kesan kepada PAS, khususnya kerana setiap orang mempunyai pengikut tersendiri.Kumpulan yang kalah, katanya, akan berasa tidak puas hati dan mungkin ada “macam-macam” cerita yang keluar.Kerana itu, katanya, dia cenderung agar tiada pertembungan berlaku di peringkat atasan parti.Terdahulu Mohd Amar diminta mengulas mengenai pertandingan dan pertembungan tajam mungkin berlaku dalam Muktamar PAS Ke-72 yang akan berlangsung pada Sept nanti.Walaupun kelihatan bahang pemilihan itu tidak ketara berbanding parti lain, beberapa petanda menunjukkan wujud dua aliran yang sedang bersaing dalam parti tersebut.Misalnya ada pemimpin Pemuda PAS negeri yang menggunakan label “kumpulan pro-DAP” kepada pihak tertentu dalam parti berkenaan. Kumpulan yang menggelarkan diri mereka Geng Ustaz pula baru-baru ini membangkitkan isu adanya cubaan “melanggar presiden” dan menganggapnya sebagai “kudis lama” dalam parti tersebut.Malah Presiden Geng Ustaz, Ahmad Dusuki Abd Rani, turut menggelar pihak yang mengganggu kepimpinan ulama sebagai “syaitan-syaitan dalam kalangan manusia dan jin”. Mohd Amar menegaskan, kepimpinan PAS memang sejak dulu tidak pernah mengawal atau menyekat sebarang pertandingan dalam parti selagi ia melalui proses dan kelayakan yang ditetapkan perlembagaan.Takkan boleh duduk diamDitanya mengenai kenyataan-kenyataan yang dilihat menggesa agar dua jawatan tertinggi PAS tidak diisi tokoh profesional, Mohd Amar berkata, perkara itu hanya pandangan peribadi pelbagai pihak apabila pemilihan tiba.Pada masa sama lepasan Universiti Birmingham di UK itu juga cenderung agar dua jawatan tertinggi PAS diisi oleh dua tokoh agamawan atau ulama.“Biasalah dalam parti memang tiada sebarang halangan. Cuma apabila nak bertanding orang ini ada pandangan, orang itu ada pandangannya, saya pun beri pandangan saya... tapi bukan arahan, sebaliknya sekadar pandangan peribadi,” katanyaPun begitu, Mohd Amar mengingatkan, sudah lama PAS tidak menyaksikan pertandingan di peringkat atasan parti itu kerana biasanya ramai yang menarik diri walaupun dicalonkan.Kecuali, katanya, jika ada kekosongan apabila penyandang berundur.Mohd Amar turut akui betapa pertembungan dalam pemilihan akan menyebabkan berlaku pergeseran dalaman seperti yang sedang dialami PKR susulan persaingan di antara Nurul Izzah Anwar dan Rafizi Ramli baru-baru ini.Katanya, pertembungan antara dua pimpinan PKR itu sangat serius dalam konteks politik semasa sekali gus menyaksikan wujud ketidakstabilan politik dalam parti-parti kerajaan Madani.Malah Mohd Amar melihat konflik itu memberi kesan besar kepada negara dan sempat mendoakan agar perwakilan PRK memenangkan Nurul Izzah kerana akan menguntungkan PAS."Masalah Nurul Izzah dan Rafizi ini (isu) besar dari segi politik kerana ia bukan sekadar pertembungan biasa melibatkan anak presiden. “Sebelum pertandingan saya doakan Nurul Izzah menang, sebab ia bagi kesan perpecahan besar."Rafizi seorang yang loose cannon, (apabila kalah) takkan duduk diam, dia akan terus membedil hingga PRU akan datang. Ini satu kelebihan kepada kita sebagai pembangkang,” katanya.Begitu juga DAP apabila Mohd Amar mentafsirkan berlaku pertembungan di antara kem Setiausaha Agung DAP, Anthony Loke, dengan veteran parti itu yang kini menjadi penasihat, Lim Guan Eng.Dalam Umno pula, kata Speaker DUN Kelantan itu lagi, konflik tidak terkecuali sehingga membawa kepada langkah Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz meninggalkan parti berkenaan dan memohon menyertai PKR.“Semua ini – kalau orang yang faham politik – akan nampak kelemahan parti-parti tersebut."Sebab itu PAS kena jaga, jangan kita buat perangai serupa (hingga) bertembung tak tentu pasal sesama kita. “Kalau kita boleh tampilkan imej yang stabil, tenang, tidak berebut jawatan dan tiada kepentingan peribadi, kitalah pilihan terbaik untuk rakyat," jelasnya

簇 #66 (包含 1 条文档)

Kredit Gambar : UTUSAN TV Strategi Tersirat dan Pergolakan Dalam: Memahami Dinamika Pemilihan PKRPemilihan Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR) yang berlangsung baru-baru ini bukan sekadar medan pertandingan jawatan, tetapi telah membuka tirai kepada satu babak politik dalaman yang penuh dengan perancangan strategik, pertarungan pengaruh dan percaturan masa depan. Apa yang kelihatan sebagai pertandingan biasa sebenarnya menyembunyikan naratif lebih kompleks—naratif yang berkait rapat dengan masa depan kepimpinan parti, penyusunan kuasa dalaman, dan hala tuju kerjasama politik menjelang Pilihan Raya Umum akan datang. Dari Rafizi vs Saifuddin ke Rafizi vs “Bayangan” Pada awalnya, tumpuan pemilihan tertumpu kepada potensi pertembungan antara Rafizi Ramli dan Setiausaha Agung PKR, Datuk Seri Saifuddin Nasution Ismail, bagi jawatan Timbalan Presiden. Namun, apabila Presiden PKR, Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim, mengusulkan agar dua jawatan tertinggi – Presiden dan Timbalan Presiden – tidak dipertandingkan, ramai menjangkakan Rafizi akan meneruskan peranannya tanpa cabaran. Suasana kelihatan tenang di permukaan, namun gelora mula dirasai di bawah arus.Apa yang berlaku selepas itu lebih menarik. Secara tiba-tiba, satu gelombang sokongan yang mengusul agar Nurul Izzah Anwar bertanding untuk jawatan Timbalan Presiden mula muncul di pelbagai cabang PKR di seluruh negara. Kenyataan demi kenyataan daripada akar umbi menyatakan sokongan terbuka kepada beliau walhal sebelum ini, hanya nama Saifuddin yang dipetik oleh media dan dianggap oleh ahli-ahli PKR sendiri sebagai satu-satunya saingan kepada Rafizi sebagai calon Timbalan Presiden. Yang lebih menarik adalah sokongan kepada Nurul Izzah ini secara jelas bukan sesuatu yang berlaku secara spontan,n, tetapi muncul secara serentak dan teratur- seolah-olah kesemua ini adalah perancangan teliti oleh satu gerakan tersusun di belakang tabir. Ini kerana UMNO? Mengapa Nurul Izzah? Mengapa sekarang? Menurut pemerhatian peribadi dan juga berdasarkan info dalaman, Rafizi dikatakan kurang bersetuju dengan cadangan kerjasama erat antara PKR dan UMNO dalam menghadapi PRU akan datang. Walaupun Pakatan Harapan (PH) telah membentuk kerajaan bersama Barisan Nasional (BN), Rafizi kekal berhati-hati. Beliau melihat risiko jangka panjang terhadap identiti politik reformis PKR jika terlalu akrab dengan UMNO, sebuah parti yang suatu ketika dahulu menjadi musuh utama perjuangan reformasi. Pandangan ini tidak semestinya selari dengan strategi politik Anwar yang lebih pragmatik—mencari jalan kembali berkuasa. Tafsiran umum adalah Rafizi telah menyusun rangkaian pengaruhnya dalam Majlis Pimpinan Pusat (MPP) dengan individu-individu yang sealiran dengannya—satu langkah yang dilihat sesetengah pihak sebagai penguasaan berpusat yang mungkin mengganggu sebarang keputusan yang bakal diambil kelak berkenaan kerjasama bersama UMNO/BN. Pergolakan Kabinet dan Dinamika KepimpinanDalam masa yang sama, spekulasi mengenai rombakan kabinet turut menambah rencah dalam naratif ini. Nama Menteri Besar Selangor, Datuk Seri Amirudin Shari dikaitkan dengan cadangan untuk dilantik sebagai Menteri Perdagangan Antarabangsa dan Industri (MITI), menggantikan Tengku Zafrul Aziz. Pelantikan ini dilihat akan menggugat kedudukan Rafizi sebagai Menteri paling kanan di dalam PKR selepas Anwar Ibrahim. Ini kerana sekiranya Amruddin dilantik sebagai Menteri MITI, Amiruddin akan muncul menyaingi Rafizi sebagai Menteri Kanan dengan portfolio yang penting di dalam kabinet. Malah, ada yang mungkin berpandangan portfolio MITI lebih berprestij daripada portfolio ekonomi bawah Rafizi,  Akhir sekali, sekiranya tafsiran politik saya betul, Nurul Izaah akan mengambil alih sebagai Menteri Besar Selangor dalam strategi yang saya beri nama Langkah Kajang 2.0. Langkah Kajang 2.0 ini bukan sahaja dijangka membuka ruang kepada Nurul Izzah menonjol sebagai pemimpin wanita yang memegang jawatan tertinggi dalam pentadbiran negeri paling maju di Malaysia. Percaturan ini dilakukan untuk mengukir imej Nurul Izzah sebagai pemimpin diterima calon Perdana Menteri kelak. 簇 #71 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
PETALING JAYA: A Cabinet reshuffle now seems inevitable, whether it be a minor tweak or a major overhaul, following the recent resignations by two ministers. But one question continues to swirl – will Datuk Seri Tengku Zafrul Abdul Aziz remain in government? Currently on a haj pilgrimage, the Investment, Trade and Industry minister has stepped down from all his Umno positions and signalled his intent to join PKR. While some tout Tengku Zafrul as a potential replacement for Datuk Seri Rafizi Ramli as the Economy minister, the looming expiry of his Senate term casts doubt over his future in Putrajaya. In Malaysian politics, little is off the table, but Tengku Zafrul’s trajectory may take a different turn. According to Universiti Malaya Political Science Department senior lecturer Dr Mohammad Tawfik Yaakub, Tengku Zafrul may be destined for a more prominent role, not at the federal level but in Selangor, the unity government’s economic engine. “I don’t see him moving to the Economy Ministry. In fact, I believe he’s being groomed for something bigger, the Selangor menteri besar post,” Tawfik told theSun via WhatsApp. “The Economy Ministry is too small compared with the Investment, Trade and Industry Ministry (Miti) or leading Selangor. His track record in driving investments fits perfectly with Selangor’s ambition as an industrial powerhouse. After all, the state contributes 25.9% of the nation’s GDP, a microcosm of Malaysia.” Tawfik added that a by-election could pave the way for Langkah Zafrul – Zafrul’s entry into state leadership. “I expect a Cabinet reshuffle soon, and with his Senate term ending, it opens the door. Current Menteri Besar Datuk Seri Amirudin Shaari holds both the Sungai Tua state and Gombak parliamentary seats. “If Amirudin moves to a federal role, it would make little sense for him to keep his state seat. A by-election in Sungai Tua could clear the path for Zafrul.” Amirudin retained the Sungai Tua seat in the 15th general election with a 5,185-vote majority, defeating Perikatan Nasional’s Muhammad Hanif Jamaluddin and independent G. Suman. Universiti Kebangsaan Malaysia professor Dr Kartini Aboo Talib believes Tengku Zafrul might stay in the Cabinet, possibly replacing Rafizi, though she doubts there would be any major shift in economic policy. “What matters is the integrity of the Economy minister. Public interest must come first, not personal or crony agendas. “We’ll have to wait for the reshuffle. The prime minister still holds the Finance Ministry portfolio, but changes could involve Miti and the Economy Ministry. Nurul Izzah Anwar might also return, given her experience.” Political analyst Dr Lim Teck Ghee agrees that Tengku Zafrul is a strong contender for the economy portfolio but cautions that technical credentials alone are not enough. “Tengku Zafrul has the financial expertise, he’s the best fit on paper. “But in our political landscape, leadership trumps technocratic ability. He’ll have limited time to make an impact. Still, his appointment could boost PKR’s image ahead of the next general election.” It was reported that Tengku Zafrul’s decision to leave Umno had impacted the party’s ministerial quota and bargaining power within the unity government, leading to calls from some Umno members for him to resign from his Cabinet position as Miti minister. However, Prime Minister Datuk Seri Anwar Ibrahim has affirmed that Tengku Zafrul would remain in his ministerial post, citing his strong performance in securing investments.

Pengarah Strategi Parti Keadilan Rakyat (PKR) Selangor, Saifuddin Shafi Muhammad berkata, sebarang rundingan perlu diurus dengan penuh beradab dan beretika terutama jika kesepakatan belum dicapai. 簇 #75 (包含 1 条文档)

⸻ 📊 Kenapa Gen Y & Gen Z Mungkin Tolak Anwar? 1. 🧠 Politik Nilai vs Politik Nostalgia 	 •	Gen Z tak terikat dengan sejarah 1998, era reformasi, atau ISA. 	 •	Mereka tak “emotionally invested” dalam perjuangan Anwar macam Gen X atau baby boomers. 	 •	Mereka lebih tanya: “Apa dia buat sekarang untuk aku?” ⸻ 2. 🎓 Tekanan Hidup Real-Time 	 •	Gaji rendah, kos rumah tinggi, peluang kerja terhad. 	 •	Bila kerajaan cakap “sabar, sedang diusahakan,” tapi realiti tak berubah… anak muda rasa dikhianati. 	 •	Mereka mahukan keputusan, bukan sekadar perjuangan. ⸻ 3. 📱 Akses Maklumat Bukan Lagi Kawalan Kerajaan 	 •	Gen Z tengok YouTube, TikTok, Reddit — bukan TV3. 	 •	Mereka nampak kegagalan, flip-flop, nepotisme, janji tinggal janji. 	 •	Bila isu Rafizi, Izzah, perlantikan politik dan “Daddykasi” muncul, kredibiliti Anwar terhakis. ⸻ 4. 🗣️ Identiti Politik Baru Sedang Terbentuk 	 •	Gen Z tak minat sangat parti, tapi isu. 	 •	Isu Palestine, climate, hak pekerja, kemiskinan bandar — siapa yang responsif, mereka sokong. 	 •	Mereka boleh sokong kiri, islamis, liberal, atau indie — asalkan genuine. ⸻ 5. ⚠️ Kekecewaan Pasca PRU15 	 •	Ramai Gen Y & Z undi PH dulu sebab tak nak rasuah dan nak perubahan. 	 •	Tapi bila dilihat: 	 •	Zahid jadi TPM 	 •	Tiada tindakan ke atas beberapa tokoh besar 	 •	Masih tiada reformasi institusi yang signifikan Mereka mula rasa: “Ini bukan Malaysia Baharu, ini Malaysia Lama pakai baju baharu.” ⸻ 🧠 Kesimpulan: Kalau Anwar dan PH terus bergantung pada naratif lama, tanpa solusi radikal untuk generasi muda, mereka akan hilang gelombang sokongan masa depan.

YOURSAY | ‘Are there no other educated and capable leaders in Umno?’ Khairy's rumoured cabinet return: Reform opportunity or political gamble? Cyclonus: Khairy Jamaluddin, better known as KJ, is an impressive intellectual (or appears to be) with lots of charisma. But this is what makes him even more dangerous. The younger crowd will trust him blindly, no matter what his agenda. Amid the 1MDB scandal, he supported jailed former prime minister Najib Abdul Razak. You would think a smart guy like him could see through Najib when the rest of the civilised world could. However, KJ put loyalty to Umno and Najib above the good of all Malaysians and Malaysia. That was very disappointing and dangerous. Forget him. GreenFalcon2290: Ah, yes, KJ is known as a “progressive and reformer”. Like Prime Minister Anwar Ibrahim and his deputy, Ahmad Zahid Hamidi? Where are the voters located, urban centres or elsewhere? Are PAS voters desperate to vote for progressive, reformer candidates? As for his remarkable qualities, they seem very common and routine for anyone working in the corporate world. Interesting? No. Milshah: Something appears to be not right. Umno should be a party where there is a good pool of educated and capable young leaders. What happened to all the educated and capable Umno leaders? I refer to another article related to the retirement age for politicians, where the young ones were supportive, but the old guard were against the idea. They (politicians) do not know when to quit and let the younger generation take over. They “cantas” (get rid of, as in trimming a branch on a tree) potential leaders, or they do not give them opportunities to lead, as they see these young leaders as threats. I’m not talking about party central committees but division leaders as well. They want the position for life and will “cantas” any young leaders who could take over from them. Then, when the party asks: Where are the young educated capable leaders? There is no one, comes the answer. Why? Because all of them have been “cantas” already. FairPlay: What’s so great about KJ? He is also an old wine in a new bottle, as the saying goes. He may not be as old as the others, but soon, he will fall into the group known as “recycle”. There is no future (whatsoever) if the politics in the country keep rebranding old and recycled wine as new wine. We have 68 years of journey as a sovereign nation. Where is the nation today when compared with the tiny red dot south of the border? Headhunter: We thought he had crossed the Rubicon (point of no return) and had moved on. He is better off if he joins the likes of outgoing Economy Minister and ex-PKR deputy president Rafizi Ramli, who recently resigned from his minister post. They can move to or form a new party. We cannot find such leaders in Umno so far, so Khairy needs to prove that he is more Islamic than PAS leaders before being accepted again by Malaysians as their leader. 簇 #79 (包含 1 条文档)

RAFIZI UMUM KEJUTAN LAGI BESAR UNTUK ANWAR DAN NURUL IZZAH
------------------------------


簇 #80 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
Image credit: MSNIn the last two years since I have been writing about politics professionally, I have met a handful of politicians – two of them are a Dato Seri and one is was a former academic – and I must say that the experience of meeting them was so banal and underwhelming, that I decided to not meet the fourth politicians who I had messaged, and have decided against meeting any politicians ever since.I remember that after meeting one of the politicians, I met my friend for a Teh Tarik, who asked me how did the meeting with the politician go ?I remember how I answered him. I told him that having Teh Tarik with him was a far more enlightening and insightful experience.The reason that that I find talking to a regular person is more enlightening and insightful than talking to all of the politicians that I have met, is that all the politicians I have met, without fail, were not at all focused-on reality, but on how to make me see them as how they wanted to me to see them.Politicians, in other words, are focused almost entirely on your perception of them, and not at all on the realities of the world.Because of that, when I talk to a politician, I found the conversation to be insipid, insightful and banal, even when the politicians were doing their best to speak in the most bombastic manner, simply because talking to them never makes you feel that you understand reality better.All it will make you do is think about the politician that you are talking to – about how smart, righteous, powerful, selfless, deep and awesome they are – and I found the experience to be a waste of time, because I generally only like to think about women, not old men.Comparatively, when you talk to regular people, they will often give you a greater insight about reality, because their mind is often in tune with the realities that they deal with.  If you want to know what the problem with the roads are, for example, talk to a lorry driver, who will not only explain to you why a problem with the road is a problem, he might even have a practical and cost-effective way of addressing the problem.The reason I am bringing up this subject is because in the first message that Rafizi released after he resigned, he said that he has a plan, and a big part of the plan entails taking politics back to the people.“I do have plans on what I want to focus on, but I want to wait for the situation to cool off.“The country’s real potential is the public. We have to go back to harnessing this potential,” Rafizi said on X.I heartily agree with this idea because I think politics is indeed best when it is regular people, who deal with the realities of life on a daily basis, participate in it, rather than the elites or a career politician, who other than manufacture your perception of him or her, is probably a person that is ill equipped to deal with reality.If you think about when politics was best in the country, you will probably see that it was best during the early days of independence, when it was mostly just regular people, who were very in tune with the realities of the world, that participated in politics. It is when regular people participated in politics that practical, insightful and effective ideas were turned into policies, which in turn powered the country forward.The problem with grassroot politics tends to be its own success – grassroot politics only comes about a big problem arises, like how the return to colonial rule enabled the condition to activate grassroot politics in the independence era -  but once the grassroot politics become successful, as our own independence era grassroot politics became successful, because it not only achieved independence for the nation, it managed to lift the masses into the country out of poverty, backwardness and illiteracy within just a couple of decades,  it will becomes institutionalised, and once it is institutionalised, it is career politicians, who become far removed from the realities of life, that will monopolise the political space in the country.Career politicians,  who participate in politics for politics sake, are almost invariably people who are focused on forming your opinion of them, or building an image, rather than someone who is focused on the realities of the world.These career politicians can’t focus on the realities of the world, not only because most of them have no real-life experience, but because that is not how they have trained their mind. These are people who do not train themselves to ask practical or reality based questions, like whether it is possible to travel from Subang Jaya on a weekday afternoon, make a drop at Sunway and another one at PJ, and return back to Subang Jaya within one and half hours. Instead, these are people who are chiefly focused and trained, to sit, dress, walk and talk in a certain way, and to also to study your expression and reactions, to see whether they have managed to convince you to believe that they know something that they don’t and are capable of something that they are not.The problem with regular people as opposed to politicians, is that regular people tend to be focused on being good, while politicians tend to be focused on winning.To join politics, you have to have the mentality of a winner or a fighter, or someone who enters the arena, together with other people just like them, to fight and defeat as many people as they can, so that you can gain as much power, authority and glory from the arena as possible.Unfortunately, regular people tend to think that this competitive spirit, where you are looking at everybody around you with the intention to fight their weak point so that you can exploit it and defeat them, to be “not good”, and thus they shy away from politics, until their circumstances and realities of life become so bad, that they will be forced to join politics.  If Rafizi truly wishes to take politics back to the people, then maybe he should think of a way to make regular people see politics just as a game – like football – where you do things like argue and criticise others for the same reason that you dribble pass or tackle a person on the football field –because it is just the nature of the game to do so and it is fun.For as long as regular people think that to criticise others and argue is something that is “not good”, they will continue to shy away from politics for as long as they can afford to.If we can only get regular people to more actively participate in politics only when the circumstances in the country becomes so bad, it is start to negatively affect the realities of common people, we are doomed to forever be firefighting, or fix a problem only when it becomes really bad, without ever reaching a stage where we will be able to refine ourselves to a finer and more exalted state.If Rafizi can just find a way to get regular people with real life experiences to engage in politics for fun and see it just as a game, perhaps we can create a more dynamic and vibrant political environment, that is focused on reality and intent on generating value, as how the politicians that arose from the grassroot during the Merdeka era created a dynamic, vibrant, reality focused and value generating culture in our politics, which shook off the country of the backwardness, lethargy and the torpor of institutionalised politics, that had infected the land for hundreds of years, and caused to rise again after declining for hundreds of years.  TheRealNehruism (nehru.sathiamoorthy@gmail.com) is a content creator under the Newswav Creator programme, where you get to express yourself, be a citizen journalist, and at the same time monetize your content & reach millions of users on Newswav. PETALING JAYA: Perikatan Nasional (PN) ditunjangi PAS dan Bersatu tidak mungkin menerima Rafizi Ramli dan Nik Nazmi Nik Ahmad yang kalah pada pemilihan PKR bulan lalu kerana mereka tiada sokongan akar umbi kuat, kata penganalisis.Felo Majlis Profesor Negara, Azmi Hassan, berkata perjuangan dua pemimpin itu juga bertentangan ideologi PN, menyebabkan mustahil untuk melihat dua bekas menteri PKR memilih gabungan tersebut walaupun sedang ‘kecewa’.“Rafizi dan Nik Nazmi tidak akan berminat untuk sertai parti lain selain PKR kerana saya tak nampak cara politik atau prinsip mereka selari dengan Bersatu apetah lagi PAS,” katanya kepada FMT

簇 #83 (包含 1 条文档)
--------------------------------------------------
This might be one of the very few jobs in Malaysia where your end date is published on the newspapers. Even in the final weeks, however, I still couldn’t explain what I do to others. 

At the Ministry of Economy, I do what the system calls “structural reforms”. The easiest way to understand is to see it as redoing an old house. It’s about looking at what makes the house—walls, layout, wiring, plumbing, flooring—and keeping what still works, discarding what no longer serves, and being open to a fundamentally new house.

Or you could just see us as the planner for the economy. 

Throughout our time here, we’ve tried to be as intentional in what we do as possible. In speeches, we avoided clichés and corny platitudes. No jargon, no generalities, no long sentences. Clarity above all. Listeners must understand every word we say and feel like they’ve learned something, without being talked down. 

In programs, we avoided shortcuts. We cold-called, did decks, and pitched to power players who wouldn’t otherwise know about Malaysia. 

In our “structural reforms”, we avoided ribbon-cutting ceremonies that are larger than the policies. Launch ceremonies are to showcase early wins. Major reforms must be rooted in an overriding rationale (see images). 

We couldn’t finish what we started. But policymaking is like writing. It is not about using 1,200 words as the first and final say on a topic, but to say enough so that the next person would know where to pick up in a long conversation. Policymaking, like writing, is about passing the baton. 

I could not have applied for this job, nor could I have prepared for it. But once I have gone through it, I walk out knowing what I never knew (see images).

To every civil servant who made space for this 29-year old to join meetings and lead policies—try, fail, fix, repeat—I hope God repays your kindness. I could only buy so many chocolates from the airport. To my team who went through the worst of times together: Let’s never do this again. We will forever be cursed with this unbreakable bond and we will never forget this even if we tried our hardest. 

And to Minister Rafizi Ramli whom I have known for 12 years. Everyone who has seen Rafizi as a minister will not question his dedication. Through this experience, I saw his idealism at full display. Only idealism would convince a person to stake everything for his country (heart attack, slipped discs, lost voice—he always turned up one week after). Above all, he showed me the value that precedes all: Courage. The inexplicable, maddening belief of doing the right thing, even when it is unpopular. I’ve seen him in many forms. This was his best. Thank you for opening the door for me. 

In all my life, this was the proudest work I’ve done. Serving my country will always be the greatest honour of my life. Thank you for seeing me on this roller-coaster.
------------------------------
